                        cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fluorinated, Sulfur-Rich, Covalent Triazine Frameworks for Enhanced Confinement of Polysulfides in Lithium-Sulfur Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Fei; Yang, Shuhao; Jiang, Guangshen; Ye, Qian; Wei, Bingqing; Wang, Hongqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">43</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">37731-37738</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium-sulfur battery represents a promising class of energy storage technol. owing to its high theor. energy d. and low cost.  However, the insulating nature, shuttling of sol. polysulfides and volumetric expansion of sulfur electrodes seriously give rise to the rapid capacity fading and low utilization.  In this work, these issues are significantly alleviated by both phys. and chem. restricting sulfur species in fluorinated porous triazine-based frameworks (FCTF-S).  One-step trimerization of perfluorinated arom. nitrile monomers with elemental sulfur allows the simultaneous formation of fluorinated triazine-based frameworks, covalent attachment of sulfur and its homogeneous distribution within the pores.  The incorporation of electroneg. fluorine in frameworks provides a strong anchoring effect to suppress the dissoln. and accelerate the conversion of polysulfides.  Together with covalent chem. binding and phys. nanopore-confinement effects, the FCTF-S demonstrates superior electrochem. performances, as compared to those of the sulfur-rich covalent triazine-based framework without fluorine (CTF-S) and porous carbon delivering only phys. confinement.  Our approach demonstrates the potential of regulating lithium-sulfur battery performances at a mol. scale promoted by the porous org. polymers with a flexible design.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoYyXAI5igXgLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lik5sjCKUW5TQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhs1amurvE&amp;md5=08c3fb34785a6b44dc77284d500895b0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201800855"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bin, D.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.-G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duan, S.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, A.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wan, L.-J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Structural Engineering of Multishelled Hollow Carbon Nanostructures for High-Performance Na-ion Battery Anode</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hard carbons for sodium-ion batteries: Structure, analysis, sustainability, and electrochemistry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dou, Xinwei; Hasa, Ivana; Saurel, Damien; Vaalma, Christoph; Wu, Liming; Buchholz, Daniel; Bresser, Dominic; Komaba, Shinichi; Passerini, Stefano</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today (Oxford, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">23</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">87-104</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MTOUAN</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Hard carbons are extensively studied for application as anode materials in sodium-ion batteries, but only recently a great interest has been focused toward the understanding of the sodium storage mechanism and the comprehension of the structure-function correlation.  Although several interesting mechanisms have been proposed, a general mechanism explaining the obsd. electrochem. processes is still missing, which is essentially originating from the remaining uncertainty on the complex hard carbons structure.  The achievement of an in-depth understanding of the processes occurring upon sodiation, however, is of great importance for a rational design of optimized anode materials.In this review, we aim at providing a comprehensive overview of the up-to-date known structural models of hard carbons and their correlation with the proposed models for the sodium-ion storage mechanisms.  In this regard, a particular focus is set on the most powerful anal. tools to study the structure of hard carbons (upon de-/sodiation) and a crit. discussion on how to interpret and perform such anal.  Targeting the eventual commercialization of hard carbon anodes for sodium-ion batteries - after having established a fundamental understanding - we close this review with a careful evaluation of potential strategies to ensure a high degree of sustainability, since this is undoubtedly a crucial parameter to take into account for the future large-scale prodn. of hard carbons.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoglanyMMwzlbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lik5sjCKUW5TQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXksV2isg%253D%253D&amp;md5=f27d15bc7c58afaf33ea74d47395ffc2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201808745"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rui, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Peering into Alloy Anodes for Sodium-ion Batteries: Current Trends, Challenges, and Opportunities</span>. <i>Adv.                         "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1039/C9EE00283A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cho, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Critical Design Factors for Kinetically Favorable P-Based Compounds Toward the Alloying with Na Ions for High-Power Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1326</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1333</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C9EE00283A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D12%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D1326-1333%26journal%3DEnergy%2BEnviron.%2BSci.%26author%3DD.%2BKim%26author%3DK.%2BZhang%26author%3DM.%2BCho%26author%3DY.%2BKang%26title%3DCritical%2BDesign%2BFactors%2Bfor%2BKinetically%2BFavorable%2BP-Based%2BCompounds%2BToward%2Bthe%2BAlloying%2Bwith%2BNa%2BIons%2Bfor%2BHigh-Power%2BSodium-ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC9EE00283A&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b07060&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC9EE00283A&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Critical design factors for kinetically favorable P-based compounds toward alloying with Na ions for high-power sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Duho; Zhang, Kai; Cho, Maenghyo; Kang, Yong-Mook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1326-1333</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">First-principles calcns. with exptl. validation enable us to radically predict and compare the electron transport, elastic softness, and thermodn. phase stabilities of black phosphorus (BP) and GeP3 to figure out the crucial factors for designing the most kinetically favorable P-based compds. toward alloying with Na ions.  From the viewpoint of electron transport, Ge is able to provide P with electrons due to the difference of electronegativity, causing GeP3 to have a significantly reduced band gap and a lower electron-hopping barrier compared to BP.  Because the structure of GeP3 looks more elastically softened than that of BP, its Na+ migration barriers in the sodiated states must be lower than those of the sodiated BP structure as proven by the higher Na+ diffusion coeffs. of GeP3.  The thermodn. phase stabilities of BP and GeP3 could be predicted by calcg. their mixing enthalpy values and thereby homogeneous bulk free energies were obtained for Na1-x(GeP3) (0.0 ≤ x ≤ 0.5) indicating that no phase sepn. occurs in the sodiated GeP3 because of an addnl. stable single-phase at x = 0.25.  By contrast, the sodiated P easily gets sepd. into NaP and Na0.5P with the same sodiation content.  The suppressed phase sepn. in GeP3 makes the Na+ distribution homogeneous as confirmed by TEM-EDS color mapping and thus contributes to increasing Na+ diffusion coeffs. because Na+ migration can be primarily interrupted by the interfaces or grain boundaries between the sepd. phases.  Taking into account three enhanced physicochem. properties, the GeP3 electrodes may well present a superior rate capability to the BP electrode, underscoring that electron transport, elastic softness, and thermodn. phase stabilities must be the most important design factors for realizing kinetically favorable P-based compds. toward alloying with Na+.  In detail, even at an ultrahigh c.d. of 20 A g-1, the capacity of the GeP3 electrode still comes to 0.197 A h g-1.  At 1 A g-1, GeP3 could maintain a discharge capacity of 0.499 A h g-1 even after 1000 cycles.  This study may provide promising guidelines for the design of alloy-based electrode materials for high power and energy SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpuohmt-cRMxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-NkWcXvcVaQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXjt1ertrk%253D&amp;md5=e99bce6c29c7ff032153d09282e7b068</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702769"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, H.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational material design for ultrafast rechargeable lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tang, Yuxin; Zhang, Yanyan; Li, Wenlong; Ma, Bing; Chen, Xiaodong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">44</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5926-5940</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) are important electrochem. energy storage devices for consumer electronics and emerging elec./hybrid vehicles.  However, one of the formidable challenges is to develop ultrafast charging LIBs with the rate capability at least one order of magnitude (&gt;10 C) higher than that of the currently commercialized LIBs.  This tutorial review presents the state-of-the-art developments in ultrafast charging LIBs by the rational design of materials.  First of all, fundamental electrochem. and related ionic/electronic conduction theories identify that the rate capability of LIBs is kinetically limited by the sluggish solid-state diffusion process in electrode materials.  Then, several aspects of the intrinsic materials, materials engineering and processing, and electrode materials architecture design towards maximizing both ionic and electronic cond. in the electrode with a short diffusion length are deliberated.  Finally, the future trends and perspectives for the ultrafast rechargeable LIBs are discussed.  Continuous rapid progress in this area is essential and urgent to endow LIBs with ultrafast charging capability to meet huge demands in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpO7WUK31gnTLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-NkWcXvcVaQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cobalt Disulfide Nanoparticles Embedded in Porous Carbonaceous Micro-Polyhedrons Interlinked by Carbon Nanotubes for Superior Lithium and Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ma, Yuan; Ma, Yanjiao; Bresser, Dominic; Ji, Yuanchun; Geiger, Dorin; Kaiser, Ute; Streb, Carsten; Varzi, Alberto; Passerini, Stefano</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7220-7231</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal sulfides are appealing electrode materials for lithium and sodium batteries owing to their high theor. capacity.  However, they are commonly characterized by rather poor cycling stability and low rate capability.  Herein, we study CoS2, serving as a model compd.  We synthesized a porous CoS2/C micro-polyhedron composite entangled in a C-nanotube-based network (CoS2-C/CNT), starting from zeolitic imidazolate frameworks-67 as a single precursor.  Following an efficient 2-step synthesis strategy, the obtained CoS2 nanoparticles are uniformly embedded in porous carbonaceous micro-polyhedrons, interwoven with CNTs to ensure high electronic cond.  The CoS2-C/CNT nanocomposite provides excellent bifunctional energy storage performance, delivering 1030 mAh/g after 120 cycles and 403 mAh/g after 200 cycles (at 100 mA/g) as electrode for Li-ion (LIBs) and Na-ion batteries (SIBs), resp.  In addn. to these high capacities, the electrodes show outstanding rate capability and excellent long-term cycling stability with a capacity retention of 80% after 500 cycles for LIBs and 90% after 200 cycles for SIBs.  In situ x-ray diffraction reveals a significant contribution of the partially graphitized carbon to the Li and at least in part also for the Na storage and the report of a 2-step conversion reaction mechanism of CoS2, eventually forming metallic Co and Li2S/Na2S.  Particularly the Li storage capability at elevated (dis-)charge rates, however, appears to be substantially pseudocapacitive, thus benefiting from the highly porous nature of the nanocomposite.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoBLKHj49Wm3bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-NkWcXvcVaQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtF2ru7nO&amp;md5=8b969d7223546e16da62fd94ca433f76</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201800930"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, H.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">CuS Microspheres with Tunable Interlayer Space and Micropore as a High-Rate and Long-Life Anode for Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Transition Metal Carbides and Nitrides in Energy Storage and Conversion</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhong Yu; Xia Xinhui; Shi Fan; Zhan Jiye; Tu Jiangping; Fan Hong Jin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1500286</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">High-performance electrode materials are the key to advances in the areas of energy conversion and storage (e.g., fuel cells and batteries).  In this Review, recent progress in the synthesis and electrochemical application of transition metal carbides (TMCs) and nitrides (TMNs) for energy storage and conversion is summarized.  Their electrochemical properties in Li-ion and Na-ion batteries as well as in supercapacitors, and electrocatalytic reactions (oxygen evolution and reduction reactions, and hydrogen evolution reaction) are discussed in association with their crystal structure/morphology/composition.  Advantages and benefits of nanostructuring (e.g., 2D MXenes) are highlighted.  Prospects of future research trends in rational design of high-performance TMCs and TMNs electrodes are provided at the end.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcRme6ZLdhR-U4vKgEt20y1XfW6udTcc2ebC6GGXAj5bybntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2snivFWisQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=ed89498c9325fb3163f754751a9201ba</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.07.009"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, H.                 10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.07.009</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D269%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D534-541%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DH.%2BC.%2BPark%26author%3DK.%2BH.%2BLee%26author%3DY.%2BW.%2BLee%26author%3DS.%2BJ.%2BKim%26author%3DD.%2BM.%2BKim%26author%3DM.%2BC.%2BKim%26author%3DK.%2BW.%2BPark%26title%3DMesoporous%2BMolybdenum%2BNitride%2BNanobelts%2Bas%2Ban%2BAnode%2Bwith%2BImproved%2BElectrochemical%2BProperties%2Bin%2BLithium%2Bion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2014.07.009&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b07060&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2014.07.009&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mesoporous molybdenum nitride nanobelts as an anode with improved electrochemical properties in lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Han-Chul; Lee, Kyung-Hoon; Lee, Young-Woo; Kim, Si-Jin; Kim, Da-Mi; Kim, Min-Cheol; Park, Kyung-Won</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">269</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">534-541</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The well-defined mesoporous nanostructure electrodes have been known to have improved lithium ion reaction properties such as the lithium ion insertion/desertion reaction, cyclability, and high rate performance.  We prepd. mesoporous molybdenum nitride nanobelts via a template-free synthesis as an anode for lithium-ion batteries.  The as-prepd. molybdenum nitride nanobelts (meso-Mo2N NBs) exhibited face-centered cubic Mo2N phase, well-defined mesoporous structure, and growth of [100] direction with 1-dimensional structure.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">2D molybdenum nitride nanosheets as anode materials for improved lithium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Liangbiao; Zhang, Kailong; Pan, Honglin; Wang, Li; Wang, Di; Dai, Weicheng; Qin, Hengfei; Li, Gaoran; Zhang, Junhao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional (2D) molybdenum nitride (MoN) nanosheets are promising anode materials for improved lithium-ion batteries.  However, the reported synthesis methods of MoN generally rely on high-temp. and complex procedures with low cost efficiency.  Herein, we report a facile one-pot synthesis of 2D MoN nanosheets at a low temp. of 400°C via a solid-state reaction of molybdenum disulfide, sulfur and sodium amide in an autoclave.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mesoporous, conductive molybdenum nitride as efficient sulfur hosts for high-performance lithium-sulfur batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jiang, Guangshen; Xu, Fei; Yang, Shuhao; Wu, Jianping; Wei, Bingqing; Wang, Hongqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">395</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">77-84</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The insulating nature of sulfur and the shuttling of polysulfides are two major fundamental issues that have to be tackled in Lithium-sulfur (Li-S) batteries, generally leading to low sulfur utilization and fast capacity decay.  Constructing sulfur hosts with both excellent cond. and efficient polysulfides immobilization is crit. to the successful implementation of Li-S batteries.  Herein, mesoporous molybdenum nitride (Mo2N) with interconnected structures is readily designed as sulfur hosts to resolve the low cond. and polysulfides dissoln. issues.  The sp. surface area and the cond. of the mesoporous Mo2N are verified to be 121 m2 g-1 and 1 × 105 S m-1, resp.  Along with its high polarity enabling the chemisorption of polysulfides, the as-obtained mesoporous Mo2N is promising as sulfur host.  The polysulfides dissoln. is efficiently suppressed owing to the fruitful nanospaces in the mesoporous Mo2N that offer more exposed polar interfaces for intensive chem. affinity/adsorption with polysulfides.  Encouragingly, the as-prepd. mesoporous, conductive and polar Mo2N with sulfur delivers superior capacity of 995 mA h g-1, long cycle stability (91.9% capacity retention after 100 cycles), superior to those of Nonporous-Mo2N/S and Mesoporous-MoO3/S.  Our results reveal that vivid engineering of metal nitrides via creating nanopores is promising for pursuing high-performance Li-S batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrkG3Z4cz9M6bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhH5Kz28-3umA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXpvFKmt78%253D&amp;md5=175415476f5dec408d4d4813a8c95042</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201702791"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flower-like MoSe<sub>2</sub> /C Composite with Expanded (0 0 2) Planes of Few-layer MoSe<sub>2</sub> as the Anode for High-Performance Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem. - Eur.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flower-like MoSe2/C Composite with Expanded (0 0 2) Planes of Few-layer MoSe2 as the Anode for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Jie; Hu, Hongxing; Qin, Furong; Zhang, Peng; Zou, Lei; Wang, Haobo; Zhang, Kai; Lai, Yanqing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">23</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">56</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14004-14010</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have caught considerable attention in last few years owing to the abundance of sodium in comparison to lithium.  The com. graphite anode is demonstrated unsuitable as an anode material for SIBs due to the larger radius of Na+ ions, whereas the transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) show great potential as anodes for SIBs because of their high achievable capacity.  The sluggish kinetics, large vol. expansion, and aggregation of those materials however results in severe decay of the electrochem. performance.  In this work, a flower-like MoSe2/C composite is synthesized with ethylenediamine and cassava starch (denoted as MoSe2/Ccas) and designed based on these principles of expanding the d-spacing of (0 0 2) planes of MoSe2 to enhance the kinetics for the intercalation-deintercalation of Na+ ions and embedding MoSe2 into the carbon matrix to enhance the cond. and restrict the vol. expansion and aggregation of MoSe2.  As a result, MoSe2/Ccas exhibits superior cycle performance and rate capability for sodium storage.  It shows durable long-life cycle capability with a reversible capacity of 360 mAh g-1 after 350 cycles at 0.5 Ag-1.  At the c.d. of 4 Ag-1, the reversible capacity is still maintained at 266 mAh g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrj4xsM_U_ep7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhH5Kz28-3umA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">N-doped C-encapsulated scale-like yolk-shell frame assembled by expanded planes few-layer MoSe2 for enhanced performance in sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Hui; Liu, Beihong; Guo, Hong; Liang, Mengfang; Zhang, Yuhao; Borjigin, Timur; Yang, Xiaofei; Wang, Lin; Sun, Xueliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To meet the pressing needs of fast development of energy and environmental science, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the promising novel generation of power storage system, due to abundant reserves and low price of sodium sources.  In this work, N-doped C-encapsulated scale-like yolk-shell structured MoSe2-C materials assembled by expanded (002) planes few-layer MoSe2 nanosheets are successfully synthesized by a facile general strategy.  The few-layer crystal fringes are no more than 4 layers.  Notably, the interlayer spacing of (002) planes is expanded to 1.15 nm, which is larger than its intrinsic value of pristine MoSe2 (0.64 nm).  Particularly, the few-layer nanosheets with expanded (002) planes are spaced-restricted growing in the inner wall and the surface of hollow carbon frame and form scale-like yolk-shell hybrid MoSe2-C structure.  When evaluated as anode for SIBs, the MoSe2-C materials show ultra-long cycling life, maintaining 378 mA h g-1 over 1000 cycles at 3 A g-1.  It also exhibits outstanding rate capability and the Coulombic efficiencies for all the rate performance reaching more than 98.3% except the first one.  The expanded (002) planes, 2D fewer-layer nanosheets and unique N-doped C-encapsulated scale-like yolk-shell frame are responsible for the enhanced electrochem. performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpJaCYb2OuSpbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhH5Kz28-3umA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtlGhs7zK&amp;md5=39debccc196db246af425a4d649fd1e8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201802745"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ali, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Asif, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchically Porous Fe<sub>2</sub>CoSe<sub>4</sub> Binary-Metal Selenide for Extraordinary Rate Performance and Durable Anode of Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Manipulation of Disodium Rhodizonate: Factors for Fast-Charge and Fast-Discharge Sodium-Ion Batteries with Long-Term Cyclability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Chengliang; Fang, Yaoguo; Xu, Yang; Liang, Liying; Zhou, Min; Zhao, Huaping; Lei, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Org. sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are one of the most promising alternatives of current com. inorg. lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) esp. in the foreseeable large-scale flexible and wearable electronics.  However, only a few reports are involving org. SIBs so far.  To achieve fast-charge and fast-discharge performance and the long-term cycling suitable for practical applications, is still challenging.  Here, important factors for high performance SIBs esp. with high capacity and long-term cyclability under fast-charge and fast-discharge process are investigated.  It is found that controlling the soly. through mol. design and detn. of the electrochem. window is essential to eliminate dissoln. of the electrode material, resulting in improved cyclability.  The results show that poly(vinylidenedifluoride) will decomp. during the charge/discharge process, indicating the significance of the binder for achieving high cyclability.  Beside of these, it is also shown that decent charge transport and ionic diffusion are beneficial to the fast-charge and fast-discharge batteries.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Comparison of electrochemical performances of olivine NaFePO4 in sodium-ion batteries and olivine LiFePO4 in lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Yujie; Xu, Yunhua; Liu, Yihang; Luo, Chao; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">780-787</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon-coated olivine NaFePO4 (C-NaFePO4) spherical particles with a uniform diam. of ∼80 nm are obtained by chem. delithiation and subsequent electrochem. sodiation of carbon-coated olivine LiFePO4 (C-LiFePO4), which is synthesized by a solvothermal method.  The C-NaFePO4 electrodes are identical (particle size, particle size distribution, surface coating, and active material loading, etc.) to C-LiFePO4 except that Li ions in C-LiFePO4 are replaced by Na ions, making them ideal for comparison of thermodn. and kinetics between C-NaFePO4 cathode in sodium-ion (Na-ion) batteries and C-LiFePO4 in lithium-ion (Li-ion) batteries.  In this paper, the equil. potentials, reaction resistances, and diffusion coeff. of Na in C-NaFePO4 are systematically investigated by using the galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique (GITT), electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS) and cyclic voltammetry (CV), and compared to those of the well-known LiFePO4 cathodes in Li-ion batteries.  Due to the lower diffusion coeff. of Na-ion and higher contact and charge transfer resistances in NaFePO4 cathodes, the rate performance of C-NaFePO4 in Na-ion batteries is much worse than that of C-LiFePO4 in Li-ion batteries.  However, the cycling stability of C-NaFePO4 is almost comparable to C-LiFePO4 by retaining 90% of its capacity even after 100 charge-discharge cycles at a charge-discharge rate of 0.1 C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrGw4RDM-VGdbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhE43KZ1FM3EQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhvVyktrrM&amp;md5=4df5515d3cde5d5a5de53206146e5111</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b02471"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, T.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">NASICON-Structured NaSn2(PO4)3 with Excellent High-Rate Properties as Anode Material for Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Pu; Ma, Jun; Wang, Tianshi; Qin, Bingsheng; Zhang, Chuanjian; Shang, Chaoqun; Zhao, Jianghui; Cui, Guanglei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6668-6674</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Advanced Li-ion batteries with high rate properties are in high demand and have generated much attention in the research community.  Here, we present a simple sol-gel and solid-state reaction to synthesize NASICON-structured NaSn2(PO4)3 as anode material for lithium-ion batteries.  The obtained material exhibits excellent cycling performance and high rate capacity for half cell and LiFePO4/NaSn2(PO4)3 full cell.  Cyclic voltammograms (CV) and galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique (GITT) were used to analyze the kinetics and thermodn. of the electrode.  Morphol. and structure evolution of the NaSn2(PO4)3 electrode after cycling were explored by transmission electron microscopy (TEM).  These results showed nanoscale Sn was uniformly dispersed in the lithium phosphate matrix during the first discharge.  It is proposed that the enhanced properties are attributed to the "in situ" formation of the ionic conductor as protective matrixes, which prevents the aggregation of nanoparticles during the cycling and provides Li+ diffusion channels in the electrode for fast electrochem. reaction.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrs6URaQqapg7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhE43KZ1FM3EQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsFWhs7vN&amp;md5=04ac0a6342cbdc3a11be309d233fe998</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-018-04190-z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Nitrogen Doped Carbon Nanofibers with Superior Rate Capability and Cyclability for Potassium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nat.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly nitrogen doped carbon nanofibers with superior rate capability and cyclability for potassium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu Yang; Zhou Min; Lei Yong; Zhang Chenglin; Fu Qun; Wu Minghong; Zhao Chengxi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1720</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-ion batteries are a promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries.  However, it is challenging to achieve fast charging/discharging and long cycle life with the current electrode materials because of the sluggish potassiation kinetics.  Here we report a soft carbon anode, namely highly nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers, with superior rate capability and cyclability.  The anode delivers reversible capacities of 248 mAh g(-1) at 25 mA g(-1) and 101 mAh g(-1) at 20 A g(-1), and retains 146 mAh g(-1) at 2 A g(-1) after 4000 cycles.  Surface-dominated K-storage is verified by quantitative kinetics analysis and theoretical investigation.  A full cell coupling the anode and Prussian blue cathode delivers a reversible capacity of 195 mAh g(-1) at 0.2 A g(-1).  Considering the cost-effectiveness and material sustainability, our work may shed some light on searching for K-storage materials with high performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcSJFZPVkzYHGDUE-swuRqsHfW6udTcc2eY0CstDPVqMF7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC1MjosVCmsA%253D%253D&amp;md5=72421c9e5cc7c2c9892fb5f83f22dcb1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.6b00061"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>138</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2838</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2848</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/jacs.6b00061</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D138%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D2838-2848%26journal%3DJ.%2BAm.%2BChem.%2BSoc.%26author%3DL.%2BS.%2BLi%26author%3DR.%2BJacobs%26author%3DP.%2BGao%26author%3DL.%2BY.%2BGan%26author%3DF.%2BWang%26author%3DD.%2BMorgan%26author%3DS.%2BJin%26title%3DOrigins%2Bof%2BLarge%2BVoltage%2BHysteresis%2Bin%2BHigh-Energy-Density%2BMetal%2BFluoride%2BLithium-ion%2BBattery%2BConversion%2BElectrodes%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fjacs.6b00061&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b07060&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fjacs.6b00061&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Origins of Large Voltage Hysteresis in High-Energy-Density Metal Fluoride Lithium-Ion Battery Conversion Electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Linsen; Jacobs, Ryan; Gao, Peng; Gan, Liyang; Wang, Feng; Morgan, Dane; Jin, Song</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">138</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2838-2848</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal fluorides and oxides can store multiple lithium ions through conversion chem. to enable high-energy-d. lithium-ion batteries.  However, their practical applications have been hindered by an unusually large voltage hysteresis between charge and discharge voltage profiles and the consequent low-energy efficiency (&lt;80%).  The phys. origins of such hysteresis are rarely studied and poorly understood.  Here we employ in situ X-ray absorption spectroscopy, transmission electron microscopy, d. functional theory calcns., and galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique to first correlate the voltage profile of iron fluoride (FeF3), a representative conversion electrode material, with evolution and spatial distribution of intermediate phases in the electrode.  The results reveal that, contrary to conventional belief, the phase evolution in the electrode is sym. during discharge and charge.  However, the spatial evolution of the electrochem. active phases, which is controlled by reaction kinetics, is different.  We further propose that the voltage hysteresis in the FeF3 electrode is kinetic in nature.  It is the result of ohmic voltage drop, reaction overpotential, and different spatial distributions of electrochem. active phases (i.e., compositional inhomogeneity).  Therefore, the large hysteresis can be expected to be mitigated by rational design and optimization of material microstructure and electrode architecture to improve the energy efficiency of lithium-ion batteries based on conversion chem.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpAXaBNz_nYGrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhE43KZ1FM3EQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitFaju7g%253D&amp;md5=c03839c8baca11359c5277c465260088</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201602567"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, B.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, J.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Preparation of two-dimensional assembled Ni-Mn-C ternary composites for high-performance all-solid-state flexible supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Xilian; Shi, Wenhui; Liu, Wenxian; Ye, Shaofeng; Yin, Ruilian; Zhang, Lin; Xu, Lixin; Chen, Minghua; Zhong, Mingqiang; Cao, Xiehong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">47</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">24086-24091</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hierarchical micro-/nano-structures assembled by two-dimensional (2D) nanomaterials are promising electrode materials for energy storage devices, owing to their unique structures and synergetic effects.  Metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) are versatile templates for various hierarchically structured nanomaterials with high-performance in energy storage applications.  However, it is still a great challenge to achieve precise control of the structure and compn. of MOF-derived nanomaterials, esp. for those composites with two or more components.  In this work, a facile strategy for the prepn. of MOF-derived 2D assembled Ni-Mn-C ternary composites, which are composed of Ni(OH)2 and MnO2 nanosheets decorated on a carbon matrix (Ni(OH)2-MnO2/C), is developed.  Due to its high surface area, good elec. cond. and the synergistic effect among components, the Ni(OH)2-MnO2/C composite exhibits excellent electrochem. performance, esp. high-rate performance (574.0 F g-1 at 40 A g-1) and cycling stability (capacitance retention of ∼87% at 2 A g-1 over 10 000 cycles).  In addn., the Ni(OH)2-MnO2/C composite-based all-solid-state supercapacitor delivers high power d., good cycling stability and excellent flexibility.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo2UMtGlKSgcLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li634iuYfSjKg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXit1Wiur%252FJ&amp;md5=d7a23ebc3690bcee9e24bbc3b2ddcfd8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1039/C9TA03391B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhuang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kaskel, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Three-Dimensional Ordered Mesoporous Cobalt Nitride for Fast-Kinetics and Stable-Cycling Lithium Storage</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>7</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">17561</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">17569</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C9TA03391B</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D7%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D17561-17569%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DG.%2BJiang%26author%3DH.%2BHan%26author%3DW.%2BZhuang%26author%3DX.%2BXu%26author%3DS.%2BKaskel%26author%3DF.%2BXu%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26title%3DThree-Dimensional%2BOrdered%2BMesoporous%2BCobalt%2BNitride%2Bfor%2BFast-Kinetics%2Band%2BStable-Cycling%2BLithium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC9TA03391B&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b07060&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC9TA03391B&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-dimensional ordered mesoporous cobalt nitride for fast-kinetics and stable-cycling lithium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jiang, Guangshen; Han, Haojie; Zhuang, Wanqi; Xu, Xiaosa; Kaskel, Stefan; Xu, Fei; Wang, Hongqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">29</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">17561-17569</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The current state-of-the-art lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) still suffer from severely sluggish kinetics due to their inferior solid-state Li+ diffusion and poor cond.  Rational design of the anode materials with 3-dimensional (3D) interconnected nanostructures and conductive skeletons, esp. with ordered mesopore architectures, is of paramount importance for LIBs.  Herein, 3D bicontinuous cubic, ordered, conductive frameworks of cobalt nitride (om-CoN) are designed and used as anodes for LIBs.  The 3D grid-like ordered mesopores (∼7.5 nm) and their very thin (&lt;6 nm) and conductive skeletons in om-CoN simultaneously permit the enhanced Li+ permeability/diffusivity and smooth electron transfer for fast kinetics.  Favorable thermodn. and fast kinetics were confirmed by the galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique and higher ratio of ion-diffusion capacity contribution and larger Li+ diffusion coeffs. from cyclic voltammetry tests for om-CoN.  As a result, it delivers a large capacity, a high rate capability and a stable specific capacity of 710 mA h g-1 after 350 cycles at 1 A g-1, far outperforming nonporous and disordered mesoporous CoN and the previously reported CoN, highlighting the significance and effectiveness of 3D ordered mesopores and cond. for achieving high-performance Li storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr2EJUvS8bM2bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li634iuYfSjKg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXht1ylurbL&amp;md5=153974817dd8ea6bab35be2797f1a378</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1039/c2ee23145j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B. A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Z. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J. K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Exceptional Electrochemical Performance of Freestanding Electrospun Carbon Nanofiber Anodes Containing Ultrafine SnO<sub>x</sub> Particles</span>. <i>Energy Environ. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">9895</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">9902</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c2ee23145j</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2012%26pages%3D9895-9902%26journal%3DEnergy%2BEnviron.%2BSci.%26author%3DB.%2BA.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BYu%26author%3DZ.%2BD.%2BHuang%26author%3DY.%2BB.%2BHe%26author%3DD.%2BJang%26author%3DW.%2BS.%2BYoon%26author%3DY.%2BW.%2BMai%26author%3DF.%2BY.%2BKang%26author%3DJ.%2BK.%2BKim%26title%3DExceptional%2BElectrochemical%2BPerformance%2Bof%2BFreestanding%2BElectrospun%2BCarbon%2BNanofiber%2BAnodes%2BContaining%2BUltrafine%2BSnOx%2BParticles%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc2ee23145j&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b07060&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc2ee23145j&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exceptional electrochemical performance of freestanding electrospun carbon nanofiber anodes containing ultrafine SnOx particles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Biao; Yu, Yang; Huang, Zhendong; He, Yan-Bing; Jang, Donghyuk; Yoon, Won-Sub; Mai, Yiu-Wing; Kang, Feiyu; Kim, Jang-Kyo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9895-9902</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">SnOx-carbon nanofiber (CNF) composites are synthesized using the electrospinning technique for use as freestanding electrodes in Li-ion batteries.  The electrodes made from the composites carbonized at 750 °C (SnOx-CNF-750) with 14.5 wt% SnOx deliver a remarkable capacity of 674 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles when discharged at 0.5 A g-1.  This result is considered the highest among those reported in the literature for anodes made from similar electrospun carbon fibers contg. SnOx nanoparticles.  An increase in carbonization temp. to 950 °C (SnOx-CNF-950) results in a significant redn. of the particle content in the fiber due to aggregation of Sn to form nanoparticles external to the fibers, with concomitant degrdn. of capacities.  The presence of amorphous SnOx particles at the at. scale embedded in the conductive CNFs is thought to be responsible for the exceptional electrochem. performance of the SnOx-CNF-750 electrodes.  These ultrafine particles facilitate the reaction Sn + xLi2O SnOx + 2xLi+ + 2xe-, making it highly reversible, which is confirmed by the growing peak currents with increasing scan rate indicated by cyclic voltammetry, and the absence of Sn-Sn bonds in the particles revealed by the extended X-ray absorption fine structure spectroscopy (EXAFS).  Both the SnOx particle size and content in the fiber play important roles in controlling the rate and cyclic performance of the SnOx-CNF composite electrodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo4hUPfyTjeN7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li634iuYfSjKg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhvVams7rI&amp;md5=4115c75b681594a3c74284e2cad62df7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA00153C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rajagopalan, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S. X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, Y.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Construction of 3D Pomegranate-Like Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/Conducting Carbon Composites for High-Power Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">9833</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">9841</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C7TA00153C</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D9833-9841%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DE.%2BWang%26author%3DW.%2BXiang%26author%3DR.%2BRajagopalan%26author%3DZ.%2BWu%26author%3DJ.%2BYang%26author%3DM.%2BChen%26author%3DB.%2BZhong%26author%3DS.%2BX.%2BDou%26author%3DS.%2BChou%26author%3DX.%2BGuo%26author%3DY.-M.%2BKang%26title%3DConstruction%2Bof%2B3D%2BPomegranate-Like%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%252FConducting%2BCarbon%2BComposites%2Bfor%2BHigh-Power%2BSodium-ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC7TA00153C&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b07060&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC7TA00153C&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Construction of 3D pomegranate-like Na3V2(PO4)3/conducting carbon composites for high-power sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Enhui; Xiang, Wei; Rajagopalan, Ranjusha; Wu, Zhenguo; Yang, Junghoon; Chen, Mingzhe; Zhong, Benhe; Dou, Shi Xue; Chou, Shulei; Guo, Xiaodong; Kang, Yong-Mook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9833-9841</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Even though Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) is regarded as one of the next-generation cathode materials in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), its undesirable rate performance due to its inherently low elec. cond. has limited its application in demanding fields such as elec. vehicles.  Motivated by this fact, the present study profitably employed a conductive carbon grown in situ to obtain an NVP@C composite with a pomegranate-like structure by a simple sol-gel assisted hydrothermal technique.  The as-prepd. NVP@C composite consists of small carbon-coated NVP particles (∼200 nm) embedded in a conductive carbon matrix, which ensures short ion diffusion distances, percolating electron/ion conduction pathways and stable structural integrity.  As a result, the pomegranate-structured NVP@C composite displayed remarkable overall electrochem. performance: a high discharge capacity (110 mA h g-1 at 1C), excellent rate capability (92 mA h g-1 even at 50C) and impressive cycling stability (capacity retention of 91.3% over 2000 cycles at 10C).  Such a feasible and beneficial design provides a good strategy for other materials that require both size redn. and high electronic/ionic cond.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGopmvZfkhUYW7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0litPXD-J6Es2A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXmsFaqsbc%253D&amp;md5=f98b856a7a181eac53ebaafb53fb24de</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6ec12bb95775c-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44'],'ref45':['cit45'],'ref46':['cit46'],'ref47':['cit47'],'ref48':['cit48']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Probing the Complexities of Structural Changes in Layered Oxide Cathode Materials for Li-Ion Batteries during Fast Charge-Discharge Cycling and Heating</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Enyuan; Wang, Xuelong; Yu, Xiqian; Yang, Xiao-Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">51</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">290-298</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACHRE4</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0001-4842</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The rechargeable lithium-ion battery (LIB) is the most promising energy storage system to power elec. vehicles with high energy d. and long cycling life.  However, in order to meet customers' demands for fast charging, the power performances of current LIBs need to be improved.  From the cathode aspect, layer-structured cathode materials are widely used in today's market and will continue to play important roles in the near future.  The high rate capability of layered cathode materials during charging and discharging is crit. to the power performance of the whole cell and the thermal stability is closely related to the safety issues.  Therefore, the in-depth understanding of structural changes of layered cathode materials during high rate charging/discharging and the thermal stability during heating are essential in developing new materials and improving current materials.  Since structural changes take place from the at. level to the whole electrode level, combination of characterization techniques covering multilength scales is quite important.  In many cases, this means using comprehensive tools involving diffraction, spectroscopy, and imaging to differentiate the surface from the bulk and to obtain structural/chem. information with different levels of spatial resoln.For example, hard X-ray spectroscopy can yield the bulk information and soft X-ray spectroscopy can give the surface information; X-ray based imaging techniques can obtain spatial resoln. of tens of nanometers, and electron-based microcopy can go to angstroms.  In addn. to challenges assocd. with different spatial resoln., the dynamic nature of structural changes during high rate cycling and heating requires characterization tools to have the capability of collecting high quality data in a time-resolved fashion.  Thanks to the advancement in synchrotron based techniques and high-resoln. electron microscopy, high temporal and spatial resolns. can now be achieved.  In this Account, we focus on the recent works studying kinetic and thermal properties of layer-structured cathode materials, esp. the structural changes during high rate cycling and the thermal stability during heating.  Advanced characterization techniques relating to the rate capability and thermal stability will be introduced.  The different structure evolution behavior of cathode materials cycled at high rate will be compared with that cycled at low rate.  Different response of individual transition metals and the inhomogeneity in chem. distribution will be discussed.  For the thermal stability, the relationship between structural changes and oxygen release will be emphatically pointed out.  In all these studies being reviewed, advanced characterization techniques are critically applied to reveal complexities at multiscale in layer-structured cathode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqvcjf1DH_-eLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh_cbnJfjixiQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtFOnsr4%253D&amp;md5=a36ac473560b142eb24679f0f6080434</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-017-00973-y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chae, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ko, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cho, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fast-charging High-energy Lithium-ion Batteries via Implantation of Amorphous Silicon Nanolayer in Edge-plane Activated Graphite Anodes</span>. <i>Nat.                 10.1038/s41467-017-00973-y</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fast-charging high-energy lithium-ion batteries via implantation of amorphous silicon nanolayer in edge-plane activated graphite anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim Namhyung; Chae Sujong; Ma Jiyoung; Ko Minseong; Cho Jaephil; Ko Minseong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
